Aero Vodochody A.101
A.101
Without any modern ground-attack aircraft, the Dual Monarchy sought to retrofit existing models to fit the role. The A.101 is the culmination of several attempts at upgrading the A.230 biplane to fill the role. Substantially larger and better armed than its predecessors, the A.101 is capable of both strafing and bombing as effectively as any of its contemporaries.
Weiss Manfréd WM.231
WM.231
Weiss Manfréd submitted the WM.23 fighter to compete with Avia's design. While its cowling-mounted, motor-driven Gebauer machine guns impressed the Committee, the B.135 was selected instead. Weiss Manfréd responded with a slight redesign, submitting it again as a dive-bomber instead to supplement the ageing fleet of A.101 biplanes in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.44
WM.44
Designed by László Varga, it was essentially a smaller, two-men version of the WM.31 series of heavy fighters and fast bombers. Like its predecessor, it was made out of both wood and metal to increase performance. It proved more than capable, albeit lightly-armoured, for close air support missions.
Phönix D.V
D.V
Adopted by the Austrian Air Force in 1933, dozens of D.Vs were provided to Albania by the Dual-Monarchy. Basic domestic production on a small scale was also begun.
Avia B.534
B.534
In 1932, Renowned Bohemian engineer František Novotný began work with the Avia company on a new all-metal biplane. This effort would culminate in the B-34, which was very nearly adopted by the Dual Monarchy over the Phönix. Not to be dissuaded, the Novotný redesigned the B-34 with a new engine and chassis, as well as a fully enclosed cockpit. Unlike its predecessor, this model, the B-534, would be adopted by the Dual Monarchy.
Avia B.135
B.135
After the success of its B-534 biplane, Avia soon began work on a cutting-edge monoplane which would ultimately culminate in the B-135. It used the Austro-Daimler V12D 860 hp engine and was equipped with a 20mm autocannon in the nose and two synchronised 8mm machine guns in the cowling, giving it great manoeuvrability and accurate fire.
Avia-Ikarus B.224
B.224
Essentially the final evolution of Novotný's design, with help from Kosta Sivčev as well as the Illyrian Ikarus company, the B.224's engine was upgraded the excellent 1000 hp Austro-Daimler V12E and the machine guns were replaced by two Gebauer 12.7mm motor-driven heavy machine guns, increasing its speed and firepower over its predecessor. Notable is the new bubble canopy for the pilot and sleek fuselage.
Avia Bf.262
Bf.262
Lagging behind in the development of jet fighters, Avia acquired a licence to produce the Bf 262 for the Fliegerkorps, replacing the German 30mm guns with locally-produced 20mm guns in their slightly-revised design.
Letov L.52
Letov L.52
L.52
L.52
When Austro-Daimler developed the U2 'Uzelac' engine, Letov produced a state-of-the-art jet fighter that would become the Monarchy's first local jet aircraft adopted into service.
Letov Š.328.v
Š.328.v
The Š.328.v was the seaplane derivative of the Š.28 series. It was armed with two forward-firing 8mm machine guns and two more in a flexible mount at the rear, and had a payload capacity of around 500kg.
Lohner-Fokker T.VIII W/C
T.VIII W/C
Lohner, a company that previously made seaplanes and flying boats for the k.u.k. Seefliegerkorps during the war, acquired the rights to produce the Fokker T.VIII for the Austro-Hungarian Navy.
Weiss Manfréd WM.442
WM.442
The WM.442 is the seaplane variant of the WM.44 made for the Seefliegerkorps, intended for Adriatic and Mediterranean anti-ship operations.
Praga E.51
E.51
Initially designed as a reconnaissance aircraft, it was quickly determined that the E.51 could be quickly adapted as a heavy fighter to counter strategic bombers.
Weiss Manfréd WM.31
WM.31
The Hungarian aviation engineer László Varga designed this 3-seat fighter around experimental gas turbine engines. However, technical difficulties arose over the engines and were replaced by two Austro-Daimler V12D instead. Notably, the WM.31 was of mixed construction.
Weiss Manfréd WM.50
WM.50
The WM.50 was a rather advanced designed for its time: The two engine push-pull configuration, twin-boom aircraft by Lázló Varga was designed to significantly improve the performance of two-engine fighters to counter high-altitude bombers.
Avia F.39
F.39
Originally developed by Fokker as a transport craft, the F.IX, the Avia company quickly saw the plane's military potential, and upon receiving a licence for the aircraft, redesigned the F.IX as a bomber, the F.39. The Dual Monarchy, lacking sufficient bombers, adopted the F.39 as a stopgap while newer models were developed.
Letov Š-50
Š-50
Intending to fill the Fliegerkorps' request for a multirole two-engine, three-man crew aircraft, Letov submitted the Š-50. However, the design did not catch interest and would never be produced, with Aero's design being eventually adopted instead.
Aero Vodochody A.300
A.300
This bomber design by Antonín Husník was, when it entered service, one of the fastest aircraft in inventory, only behind the newly-adopted B.135 fighter. Fast and with a good payload, it proved to be a versatile bomber and reconnaissance aircraft.
Weiss Manfréd WM.311
WM.311
The WM.31 was quickly adapted to perform the role of a fast, tactical bomber by weakening its offensive armament and improving its payload capacity.
Letov L.11
L.11
Based on a jet fighter design by the Bayerische Flugzeugwerke, the L.11 adapted the design into a fast and light jet bomber for multiple roles, hoping to replace the Monarchy's fleet of older prop-driven tactical bombers.
Aero L.44
L.44
With the reliability of jet engines increasing and competition ever-so fierce, Aero tackled the challenge to design a next-generation fast-bomber, culminating into the L.44 fast bomber.
Avia-Dornier Do.19
Do.19
Lacking designs for strategic bombers, Avia purchased a number of Dornier four-engine bombers to showcase their potential to the air force.
Avia-Junkers Ju.290
Ju.290
Avia acquired a number of Ju.290 to supplement the small fleet of Do.19 in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.65
WM.65
Lázló Varga's four-engine bomber design was the first domestically-produced heavy bomber of its kind in the Empire.
Aero-Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16
FF.16
The German Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16 would be adopted as Austria's long-range bomber, locally produced by Aero Vodochody.

Phönix D.V
D.V
With the Weltkrieg's end, the Phönix company's planned redesign of its famous D.III biplane, with the expected designation 'D.IV', never came to pass. In 1931, however, the company would resurrect the D.IV moniker with the unveiling of an entirely new biplane featuring then cutting-edge specifications. An upgraded variant of the craft, designated D.V, was adopted by the Dual Monarchy in 1933.

Sabca-Caproni 47
S.47
This close air support aircraft suffered in 1940 from an insufficient speed, making it an easy target, and an insufficient payload, making the destruction of the bridges of the Canal Albert impossible for the poor pilots assigned on those last chance missions.
Renard 37 B 14N
R-37 B
The Renard 37 B is a biplane variant of the R37 for ground attacks, as only a prototype of the fighter version was built, it stayed on paper and was never made.

Renard 37 Aéronaval
R-37 DC AN

Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Bf 110

Caproni Ca.331
Ca.331
Renard 42
R-42
The R-42 is a twin fighter long range variant of the R-36 and subsequent designs (R-38, R-40), an idea later developed in the American F-82 Twin Mustang. Due to the war it was only sketched.
LACAB GR.8
GR.8
The GR.8, nicknamed 'Doryphore' (meaning 'Potato Bug' because of its poor flying capabilities) was made in order to serve as a multipurpose aircraft for the Belgian air force. Supposed to serve as a bomber, a reconnaissance aircraft and a heavy fighter it followed the ludicrous demands of the Belgian army to the letter... and was consequently bad in all of those roles.
SABCA S.45
SABCA S.45
The SABCA S.45 is a licence built Caproni Ca.135 to enable a greater production of planes than Italy's limited capabilities. With this experience in bomber building the Belgian could have easily built more of those for their own use, but they never did.
Renard R.35B
R.35B
Dornier Do 19
Do 19
Hansa-Brandenburg Hb 177
Hb 177
Renard R.32
R.32
Caproni Ca.311
Ca.311
Curtiss CW-19R
CW-19R
Aero Vodochody A.101
A.101
Without any modern ground-attack aircraft, the Dual Monarchy sought to retrofit existing models to fit the role. The A.101 is the culmination of several attempts at upgrading the A.230 biplane to fill the role. Substantially larger and better armed than its predecessors, the A.101 is capable of both strafing and bombing as effectively as any of its contemporaries.
Weiss Manfréd WM.231
WM.231
Weiss Manfréd submitted the WM.23 fighter to compete with Avia's design. While its cowling-mounted, motor-driven Gebauer machine guns impressed the Committee, the B.135 was selected instead. Weiss Manfréd responded with a slight redesign, submitting it again as a dive-bomber instead to supplement the ageing fleet of A.101 biplanes in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.44
WM.44
Designed by László Varga, it was essentially a smaller, two-men version of the WM.31 series of heavy fighters and fast bombers. Like its predecessor, it was made out of both wood and metal to increase performance. It proved more than capable, albeit lightly-armoured, for close air support missions.
Phönix D.V
D.V
With the Weltkrieg's end, the Phönix company's planned redesign of its famous D.III biplane, with the expected designation 'D.IV', never came to pass. In 1931, however, the company would resurrect the D.IV moniker with the unveiling of an entirely new biplane featuring then cutting-edge specifications. An upgraded variant of the craft, designated D.V, was adopted by the Dual Monarchy in 1933.
Avia B.534
B.534
In 1932, Renowned Bohemian engineer František Novotný began work with the Avia company on a new all-metal biplane. This effort would culminate in the B-34, which was very nearly adopted by the Dual Monarchy over the Phönix. Not to be dissuaded, the Novotný redesigned the B-34 with a new engine and chassis, as well as a fully enclosed cockpit. Unlike its predecessor, this model, the B-534, would be adopted by the Dual Monarchy.
Avia B.135
B.135
After the success of its B-534 biplane, Avia soon began work on a cutting-edge monoplane which would ultimately culminate in the B-135. It used the Austro-Daimler V12D 860 hp engine and was equipped with a 20mm autocannon in the nose and two synchronised 8mm machine guns in the cowling, giving it great manoeuvrability and accurate fire.
Avia-Ikarus B.224
B.224
Essentially the final evolution of Novotný's design, with help from Kosta Sivčev as well as the Illyrian Ikarus company, the B.224's engine was upgraded the excellent 1000 hp Austro-Daimler V12E and the machine guns were replaced by two Gebauer 12.7mm motor-driven heavy machine guns, increasing its speed and firepower over its predecessor. Notable is the new bubble canopy for the pilot and sleek fuselage.
Avia Bf.262
Bf.262
Lagging behind in the development of jet fighters, Avia acquired a licence to produce the Bf 262 for the Fliegerkorps, replacing the German 30mm guns with locally-produced 20mm guns in their slightly-revised design.
Letov L.52
Letov L.52
L.52
L.52
When Austro-Daimler developed the U2 'Uzelac' engine, Letov produced a state-of-the-art jet fighter that would become the Monarchy's first local jet aircraft adopted into service.
Letov Š.328.v
Š.328.v
The Š.328.v was the seaplane derivative of the Š.28 series. It was armed with two forward-firing 8mm machine guns and two more in a flexible mount at the rear, and had a payload capacity of around 500kg.
Lohner-Fokker T.VIII W/C
T.VIII W/C
Lohner, a company that previously made seaplanes and flying boats for the k.u.k. Seefliegerkorps during the war, acquired the rights to produce the Fokker T.VIII for the Austro-Hungarian Navy.
Weiss Manfréd WM.442
WM.442
The WM.442 is the seaplane variant of the WM.44 made for the Seefliegerkorps, intended for Adriatic and Mediterranean anti-ship operations.
Praga E.51
E.51
Initially designed as a reconnaissance aircraft, it was quickly determined that the E.51 could be quickly adapted as a heavy fighter to counter strategic bombers.
Weiss Manfréd WM.31
WM.31
The Hungarian aviation engineer László Varga designed this 3-seat fighter around experimental gas turbine engines. However, technical difficulties arose over the engines and were replaced by two Austro-Daimler V12D instead. Notably, the WM.31 was of mixed construction.
Weiss Manfréd WM.50
WM.50
The WM.50 was a rather advanced designed for its time: The two engine push-pull configuration, twin-boom aircraft by Lázló Varga was designed to significantly improve the performance of two-engine fighters to counter high-altitude bombers.
Avia F.39
F.39
Originally developed by Fokker as a transport craft, the F.IX, the Avia company quickly saw the plane's military potential, and upon receiving a licence for the aircraft, redesigned the F.IX as a bomber, the F.39. The Dual Monarchy, lacking sufficient bombers, adopted the F.39 as a stopgap while newer models were developed.
Letov Š-50
Š-50
Intending to fill the Fliegerkorps' request for a multirole two-engine, three-man crew aircraft, Letov submitted the Š-50. However, the design did not catch interest and would never be produced, with Aero's design being eventually adopted instead.
Aero Vodochody A.300
A.300
This bomber design by Antonín Husník was, when it entered service, one of the fastest aircraft in inventory, only behind the newly-adopted B.135 fighter. Fast and with a good payload, it proved to be a versatile bomber and reconnaissance aircraft.
Weiss Manfréd WM.311
WM.311
The WM.31 was quickly adapted to perform the role of a fast, tactical bomber by weakening its offensive armament and improving its payload capacity.
Letov L.11
L.11
Based on a jet fighter design by the Bayerische Flugzeugwerke, the L.11 adapted the design into a fast and light jet bomber for multiple roles, hoping to replace the Monarchy's fleet of older prop-driven tactical bombers.
Aero L.44
L.44
With the reliability of jet engines increasing and competition ever-so fierce, Aero tackled the challenge to design a next-generation fast-bomber, culminating into the L.44 fast bomber.
Avia-Dornier Do.19
Do.19
Lacking designs for strategic bombers, Avia purchased a number of Dornier four-engine bombers to showcase their potential to the air force.
Avia-Junkers Ju.290
Ju.290
Avia acquired a number of Ju.290 to supplement the small fleet of Do.19 in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.65
WM.65
Lázló Varga's four-engine bomber design was the first domestically-produced heavy bomber of its kind in the Empire.
Aero-Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16
FF.16
The German Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16 would be adopted as Austria's long-range bomber, locally produced by Aero Vodochody.
Weiss Manfréd WM.21
WM.21
Praga E.55

Aero A.204

Vultee V-11

PZL.23 Karaś

DAR 10 'Bekas'
DAR 10
DAR 13
DAR 13
Avia B-34
B-34
When the Avia company's B-34 design was passed over by the Dual Monarchy, the company looked to the export market to recuperate its investment. Lacking any modern biplanes, Bulgaria adopted the B.34 in 1934.
Avia B.534
B.534
In 1932, Renowned Bohemian engineer František Novotný began work with the Avia company on a new all-metal biplane. This effort would culminate in the B-34, which was very nearly adopted by the Dual Monarchy over the Phönix. Not to be dissuaded, the Novotný redesigned the B-34 with a new engine and chassis, as well as a fully enclosed cockpit. Like the B-34, this model was also adopted by the Bulgarians, and unlike its predecessor, the B-534 was also adopted by the Dual Monarchy.
DAR 11 'Lyastovitsa'
DAR 11
After the success of its B-534 biplane, Avia soon began work on a cutting-edge monoplane which would ultimately culminate in the B-135. It used the Austro-Daimler V12D 860 hp engine and was equipped with a 20mm autocannon in the nose and two synchronised 8mm machine guns in the cowling, giving it great manoeuvrability and accurate fire. The DAR company acquired the right to produce the craft within Bulgaria due to its impressive performance in Habsburg service. Slight modifications were made by the DAR company, but the craft remains essentially the same.
DAR 12
DAR 12
When DAR chief designer Zvetan Lazarov's DAR-10A based fighter was rejected by the company in favour of a domestically modified derivative of the Avia company's B-135, he and his team went back to the drawing board entirely, ultimately designing an entirely new high-altitude fighter, the first entirely domestically-produced Bulgarian aircraft to feature a pressurised cockpit. The fighter was accepted into Bulgarian service as the DAR-12.
DAR 14
DAR 14
Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen Ff 195
Ff 195
KB-11 'Fazan'
KB-11
Originally meant to serve in a reconnaissance and light attack role, the KB-11 was repurposed as a naval patrol craft.

Arkhangelsky Ar-2
Ar-2
Unsatisfied with Austrian and German bomber designs, and their high price tag, Bulgaria looked further afield. To fill the medium bomber role, it negotiated to produce the Arkhangelsky Ar-2 under licence from the Russian Republic.
Yermolaev Er-2
Er-2
Tupolev Tu-10
Tu-10
Avia-Dornier Do.19
Do.19
Lacking designs for strategic bombers, Avia purchased a number of Dornier four-engine bombers to showcase their potential to the air force. The design was later licensed to Bulgaria.
Bloch MB.165
MB.165
Unsatisfied with Austrian and German bomber designs, and their high price tag, Bulgaria looked further afield. To fill the heavy bomber role, it negotiated to produce the Bloch MB.165 under licence from France.

KB-5 'Chuchuliga' III

KB-6 Papagal
KB-6
To meet the Bulgarian air force's requirements for a new closed-cabin long-distance reconnaissance craft, the Caproni company's Bulgarian subsidiary made several important modifications to its successful 309 'Ghibli' craft of a few years earlier.

Zhongyun-1
Zhongyun-1
A Chinese domestic development of the American Douglas DC-2, the Zhongyun became the crowning achievement of the CAMCO (Central Aircraft Manufacturing Company) of China.

Aero Vodochody A.101
A.101
Without any modern ground-attack aircraft, the Dual Monarchy sought to retrofit existing models to fit the role. The A.101 is the culmination of several attempts at upgrading the A.230 biplane to fill the role. Substantially larger and better armed than its predecessors, the A.101 is capable of both strafing and bombing as effectively as any of its contemporaries.
Weiss Manfréd WM.231
WM.231
Weiss Manfréd submitted the WM.23 fighter to compete with Avia's design. While its cowling-mounted, motor-driven Gebauer machine guns impressed the Committee, the B.135 was selected instead. Weiss Manfréd responded with a slight redesign, submitting it again as a dive-bomber instead to supplement the ageing fleet of A.101 biplanes in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.44
WM.44
Designed by László Varga, it was essentially a smaller, two-men version of the WM.31 series of heavy fighters and fast bombers. Like its predecessor, it was made out of both wood and metal to increase performance. It proved more than capable, albeit lightly-armoured, for close air support missions.
Phönix D.V
D.V
With the Weltkrieg's end, the Phönix company's planned redesign of its famous D.III biplane, with the expected designation 'D.IV', never came to pass. In 1931, however, the company would resurrect the D.IV moniker with the unveiling of an entirely new biplane featuring then cutting-edge specifications. An upgraded variant of the craft, designated D.V, was adopted by the Dual Monarchy in 1933.
Avia B.534
B.534
In 1932, Renowned Bohemian engineer František Novotný began work with the Avia company on a new all-metal biplane. This effort would culminate in the B-34, which was very nearly adopted by the Dual Monarchy over the Phönix. Not to be dissuaded, the Novotný redesigned the B-34 with a new engine and chassis, as well as a fully enclosed cockpit. Unlike its predecessor, this model, the B-534, would be adopted by the Dual Monarchy.
Avia B.135
B.135
After the success of its B-534 biplane, Avia soon began work on a cutting-edge monoplane which would ultimately culminate in the B-135. It used the Austro-Daimler V12D 860 hp engine and was equipped with a 20mm autocannon in the nose and two synchronised 8mm machine guns in the cowling, giving it great manoeuvrability and accurate fire.
Avia-Ikarus B.224
B.224
Essentially the final evolution of Novotný's design, with help from Kosta Sivčev as well as the Illyrian Ikarus company, the B.224's engine was upgraded the excellent 1000 hp Austro-Daimler V12E and the machine guns were replaced by two Gebauer 12.7mm motor-driven heavy machine guns, increasing its speed and firepower over its predecessor. Notable is the new bubble canopy for the pilot and sleek fuselage.
Avia Bf.262
Bf.262
Lagging behind in the development of jet fighters, Avia acquired a licence to produce the Bf 262 for the Fliegerkorps, replacing the German 30mm guns with locally-produced 20mm guns in their slightly-revised design.
Letov L.52
Letov L.52
L.52
L.52
When Austro-Daimler developed the U2 'Uzelac' engine, Letov produced a state-of-the-art jet fighter that would become the Monarchy's first local jet aircraft adopted into service.
Letov Š.328.v
Š.328.v
The Š.328.v was the seaplane derivative of the Š.28 series. It was armed with two forward-firing 8mm machine guns and two more in a flexible mount at the rear, and had a payload capacity of around 500kg.
Lohner-Fokker T.VIII W/C
T.VIII W/C
Lohner, a company that previously made seaplanes and flying boats for the k.u.k. Seefliegerkorps during the war, acquired the rights to produce the Fokker T.VIII for the Austro-Hungarian Navy.
Weiss Manfréd WM.442
WM.442
The WM.442 is the seaplane variant of the WM.44 made for the Seefliegerkorps, intended for Adriatic and Mediterranean anti-ship operations.
Praga E.51
E.51
Initially designed as a reconnaissance aircraft, it was quickly determined that the E.51 could be quickly adapted as a heavy fighter to counter strategic bombers.
Weiss Manfréd WM.31
WM.31
The Hungarian aviation engineer László Varga designed this 3-seat fighter around experimental gas turbine engines. However, technical difficulties arose over the engines and were replaced by two Austro-Daimler V12D instead. Notably, the WM.31 was of mixed construction.
Weiss Manfréd WM.50
WM.50
The WM.50 was a rather advanced designed for its time: The two engine push-pull configuration, twin-boom aircraft by Lázló Varga was designed to significantly improve the performance of two-engine fighters to counter high-altitude bombers.
Avia F.39
F.39
Originally developed by Fokker as a transport craft, the F.IX, the Avia company quickly saw the plane's military potential, and upon receiving a licence for the aircraft, redesigned the F.IX as a bomber, the F.39. The Dual Monarchy, lacking sufficient bombers, adopted the F.39 as a stopgap while newer models were developed.
Letov Š-50
Š-50
Intending to fill the Fliegerkorps' request for a multirole two-engine, three-man crew aircraft, Letov submitted the Š-50. However, the design did not catch interest and would never be produced, with Aero's design being eventually adopted instead.
Aero Vodochody A.300
A.300
This bomber design by Antonín Husník was, when it entered service, one of the fastest aircraft in inventory, only behind the newly-adopted B.135 fighter. Fast and with a good payload, it proved to be a versatile bomber and reconnaissance aircraft.
Weiss Manfréd WM.311
WM.311
The WM.31 was quickly adapted to perform the role of a fast, tactical bomber by weakening its offensive armament and improving its payload capacity.
Letov L.11
L.11
Based on a jet fighter design by the Bayerische Flugzeugwerke, the L.11 adapted the design into a fast and light jet bomber for multiple roles, hoping to replace the Monarchy's fleet of older prop-driven tactical bombers.
Aero L.44
L.44
With the reliability of jet engines increasing and competition ever-so fierce, Aero tackled the challenge to design a next-generation fast-bomber, culminating into the L.44 fast bomber.
Avia-Dornier Do.19
Do.19
Lacking designs for strategic bombers, Avia purchased a number of Dornier four-engine bombers to showcase their potential to the air force.
Avia-Junkers Ju.290
Ju.290
Avia acquired a number of Ju.290 to supplement the small fleet of Do.19 in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.65
WM.65
Lázló Varga's four-engine bomber design was the first domestically-produced heavy bomber of its kind in the Empire.
Aero-Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16
FF.16
The German Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16 would be adopted as Austria's long-range bomber, locally produced by Aero Vodochody.
Weiss Manfréd WM.21
WM.21
Praga E.55
E.55
Aero A.204
A.204

Fokker D.XVII
D.XVII
Fokker D.XXI
D.XXI
The Fokker D.XXI was a low-wing monoplane fighter aircraft. It was designed in 1935 by Fokker around requirements laid out by the Royal Netherlands East Indies Army Air Force.\nThe main armament consisted of two pairs of 7.92mm M36 FN-Browning machine guns, two housed within the wings and the other pair within the forward fuselage, requiring the latter to shoot through the propeller blades; the fuselage guns carried 500 rounds each while the wing-mounted guns had 300 rounds each.
Koolhoven F.K.58
F.K. 58
The Koolhoven F.K.58 was a single engine, interceptor-fighter aircraft designed and manufactured by N.V. Koolhoven.\nIts armament consisted of 4 7.5mm guns. It had a retractable landing gear and was equipped with a more powerful 1080hp engine, allowing the plane to reach speeds of up to 505 km/h with an operational range of 750km.
De Schelde S.21
S.21
The De Schelde S.21 was a single-seat, single-engine, pusher monoplane designed by Koninklijke de Schelde N.V.\nThe S.21 was of all-metal construction, and featured an inverted gull wing, with the aircraft's tail carried on twin booms. The compact fuselage nacelle carried the pilot, engine and the aircraft's armament.\nArmament consisted of a single Madsen 23 mm cannon on a flexible mount in the nose and four 7.9 mm FN-Browning machine guns in the side of the nacelle.

Fokker T.VI (Ontwerp 115)
T.VI (Ontwerp 115)
Between August 1934 and February 1935, work began on the Ontwerp 115.\nThe Ontwerp 115 was of a four engined low-wing design with retractable landing gear and a twin rudder. The aircraft would have had four radial engines with performance calculated with the Gnome-Rhóne 14Krfs at 900Hp, the 14Krsd at 1110Hp, and the Wright Cyclone SFR-1820-F2 at 712Hp. The propellers would have been three bladed and adjustable in-flight. Bombing capacity was projected at two tonnes.

SAI KZ IIA
KZ IIA
Within months of its founding, SAI, Skandinavisk Aero Industri, founded by two found technically proficient aircraft enthusiasts, produced two different sport planes. Their second model drew interest from the Danish military, which eventually contracted for the production of a ground attack variant on the craft.

Fokker-VL C.X III
C.X III
Adopted by the Dutch in 1933, the Fokker C.X was designed fly low to the ground to avoid anti-aircraft fire and as such had a low stall speed. The Finnish-built series III variant had a slightly modified chassis and redesigned wings as well as a new engine.
Fokker C.XIII
C.XIII
SAAB A 21
A 21
The Saab A-21 was first a fighter named J 21, but because it shown an inadequate performance for its fighter role. Despite this, the Saab design bureau realised its cell would be an excellent platform for an attacker. Its unique push-pull configuration, its powerful engine and the choice of loadout make it a powerful CAS.
Gloster Kukko
Kukko
The Kukko is a modified licence-produced Gloster Gamecock Mk II with a new German engine.
VL Myrsky
Myrsky
In the 1930s, Finland realised that it was rapidly falling behind its allies and enemies alike in fighter designs, lacking a steel-framed monoplane entirely. The Myrsky was designed by the Finnish state aircraft factory on the basis of German designs and featuring a Canadian engine.
VL Humu
Humu
While the Brewster Buffalo carrier fighter was initially rejected for US service and redesigned, the Finnish were immediately interested in the Brewster company's initial model. Before any prototype had ever been produced, Finland placed an order for several Buffalos. Upon arrival in Finland, the planes were retrofitted in their entirety.
VL Pyörremyrsky
Pyörremyrsky
The Pyörremyrsky was designed around later models of the Focke-Wulf Fw 190 with substantial changes made to improve the craft's agility, range, and armaments. The Pyörremyrsky is a remarkably quick and manoeuvrable fighter.

Blackburn Ripon
Ripon
The Blackburn Ripon is truly a sight to behold in Finnish service. This is not because the craft is a particularly spectacular naval bomber, but because the Ripon was indeed produced by the Blackburn Union state aircraft company in the syndicalist Union of Britain. How Finland managed to purchase the craft and gain approval and the tooling necessary to license-produce the craft is highly speculated at. The Finnish Ripon is of the Ripon IIF design.
VL Kotka
Kotka
Originally conceived of as a cheaper alternative to the Ripon, the Kotka outperforms the Ripon in nearly every way. Fitted with a new Canadian engine, the Kotka is both fast and capable of low level-low speed flight without stalling - essential to torpedo bombing.
Hansa-Brandenburg 115
Hb 115
VL Tähti
Tähti
Developed from the Canadian Beaufort medium bomber in line with Canada's own Beaufighter design, the VL Tähti has been significantly lightened and its armaments and engine retrofitted for its new role. Though, unlike the Canadian Beaufighter, the bombardier's compartment has not been removed. Instead, the Tähti features a rotating front turret.
Petlyakov Pe-3
Pe-3
Noting the success of Communard and British heavy fighter designs, in 1941 famed aircraft designer Vladimir Petlyakov and his eponymous aerospace firm began work on a fighter variant of the earlier Pe-2 medium bomber. As with many Russian designs, despite hostility between Russia and Finland, the Finnish government contracted the Petlyakov for a substantial number of the new aircraft.
VL Vihuri
Vihuri
While some accuse the Finnish of copying the design of the Union of Britain's 'Mosquito', the Finnish 'Vihuri' is indeed a Finnish design taking cues from German, Russian, Entente, and Syndicalist models.
Avro VL Anson
Anson
The Avro Anson is a medium bomber built from the Canadian airliner, the Avro 652. Unable to afford modern German designs, in 1935, the Finnish opted to adopt the Anson as a stopgap solution to their lack of bomber craft.
Bristol-VL Blenheim
Blenheim
The Blenheim medium bomber is Canada's first all-metal bomber. It was adopted by the Finish Air Force following the surprising success of the Anson, which impressed the country's leadership with Canadian aircraft.
Tupelov SB 2M-103
SB 2M-103
Before the development of the Tupelov SB, Russian firms lagged behind their western counterparts in modern medium-bomber designs. The trials and tribulations of the SB, however, injected much needed innovation into the country. The 103 features several improvements over older production models. While the Finnish adopted variant is not, strictly speaking, a true 103, Finnish SBs have been similarly retrofitted.
Arkhangelsky SBB-2
SBB-2
Based on a late model Tupelov SB, the Arkhangelsky designed the new SB-RK in late 1940 as a replacement for the SB adapted to dive-bombing rather than low level-high speed attacks. The SB-RK was later renamed to SBB and with the prototype's rejection by the Russian military, the SBB was redesigned, with the new craft designated SBB-2. The SBB-2 was offered to several foreign governments, with the Finnish securing a licence to produce the aircraft.

SNCASO SO.4000

Potez Po.542

SNCAO CAO.700
CAO.700
Aero Vodochody A.101
A.101
Without any modern ground-attack aircraft, the Dual Monarchy sought to retrofit existing models to fit the role. The A.101 is the culmination of several attempts at upgrading the A.230 biplane to fill the role. Substantially larger and better armed than its predecessors, the A.101 is capable of both strafing and bombing as effectively as any of its contemporaries.
Weiss Manfréd WM.231
WM.231
Weiss Manfréd submitted the WM.23 fighter to compete with Avia's design. While its cowling-mounted, motor-driven Gebauer machine guns impressed the Committee, the B.135 was selected instead. Weiss Manfréd responded with a slight redesign, submitting it again as a dive-bomber instead to supplement the ageing fleet of A.101 biplanes in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.44
WM.44
Designed by László Varga, it was essentially a smaller, two-men version of the WM.31 series of heavy fighters and fast bombers. Like its predecessor, it was made out of both wood and metal to increase performance. It proved more than capable, albeit lightly-armoured, for close air support missions.
Phönix D.V
D.V
With the Weltkrieg's end, the Phönix company's planned redesign of its famous D.III biplane, with the expected designation 'D.IV', never came to pass. In 1931, however, the company would resurrect the D.IV moniker with the unveiling of an entirely new biplane featuring then cutting-edge specifications. An upgraded variant of the craft, designated D.V, was adopted by the Dual Monarchy in 1933.
Avia B.534
B.534
In 1932, Renowned Bohemian engineer František Novotný began work with the Avia company on a new all-metal biplane. This effort would culminate in the B-34, which was very nearly adopted by the Dual Monarchy over the Phönix. Not to be dissuaded, the Novotný redesigned the B-34 with a new engine and chassis, as well as a fully enclosed cockpit. Unlike its predecessor, this model, the B-534, would be adopted by the Dual Monarchy.
Avia B.135
B.135
After the success of its B-534 biplane, Avia soon began work on a cutting-edge monoplane which would ultimately culminate in the B-135. It used the Austro-Daimler V12D 860 hp engine and was equipped with a 20mm autocannon in the nose and two synchronised 8mm machine guns in the cowling, giving it great manoeuvrability and accurate fire.
Avia-Ikarus B.224
B.224
Essentially the final evolution of Novotný's design, with help from Kosta Sivčev as well as the Illyrian Ikarus company, the B.224's engine was upgraded the excellent 1000 hp Austro-Daimler V12E and the machine guns were replaced by two Gebauer 12.7mm motor-driven heavy machine guns, increasing its speed and firepower over its predecessor. Notable is the new bubble canopy for the pilot and sleek fuselage.
Avia Bf.262
Bf.262
Lagging behind in the development of jet fighters, Avia acquired a licence to produce the Bf 262 for the Fliegerkorps, replacing the German 30mm guns with locally-produced 20mm guns in their slightly-revised design.
Letov L.52
Letov L.52
L.52
L.52
When Austro-Daimler developed the U2 'Uzelac' engine, Letov produced a state-of-the-art jet fighter that would become the Monarchy's first local jet aircraft adopted into service.
Letov Š.328.v
Š.328.v
The Š.328.v was the seaplane derivative of the Š.28 series. It was armed with two forward-firing 8mm machine guns and two more in a flexible mount at the rear, and had a payload capacity of around 500kg.
Lohner-Fokker T.VIII W/C
T.VIII W/C
Lohner, a company that previously made seaplanes and flying boats for the k.u.k. Seefliegerkorps during the war, acquired the rights to produce the Fokker T.VIII for the Austro-Hungarian Navy.
Weiss Manfréd WM.442
WM.442
The WM.442 is the seaplane variant of the WM.44 made for the Seefliegerkorps, intended for Adriatic and Mediterranean anti-ship operations.
Praga E.51
E.51
Initially designed as a reconnaissance aircraft, it was quickly determined that the E.51 could be quickly adapted as a heavy fighter to counter strategic bombers.
Weiss Manfréd WM.31
WM.31
The Hungarian aviation engineer László Varga designed this 3-seat fighter around experimental gas turbine engines. However, technical difficulties arose over the engines and were replaced by two Austro-Daimler V12D instead. Notably, the WM.31 was of mixed construction.
Weiss Manfréd WM.50
WM.50
The WM.50 was a rather advanced designed for its time: The two engine push-pull configuration, twin-boom aircraft by Lázló Varga was designed to significantly improve the performance of two-engine fighters to counter high-altitude bombers.
Avia F.39
F.39
Originally developed by Fokker as a transport craft, the F.IX, the Avia company quickly saw the plane's military potential, and upon receiving a licence for the aircraft, redesigned the F.IX as a bomber, the F.39. The Dual Monarchy, lacking sufficient bombers, adopted the F.39 as a stopgap while newer models were developed.
Letov Š-50
Š-50
Intending to fill the Fliegerkorps' request for a multirole two-engine, three-man crew aircraft, Letov submitted the Š-50. However, the design did not catch interest and would never be produced, with Aero's design being eventually adopted instead.
Aero Vodochody A.300
A.300
This bomber design by Antonín Husník was, when it entered service, one of the fastest aircraft in inventory, only behind the newly-adopted B.135 fighter. Fast and with a good payload, it proved to be a versatile bomber and reconnaissance aircraft.
Weiss Manfréd WM.311
WM.311
The WM.31 was quickly adapted to perform the role of a fast, tactical bomber by weakening its offensive armament and improving its payload capacity.
Letov L.11
L.11
Based on a jet fighter design by the Bayerische Flugzeugwerke, the L.11 adapted the design into a fast and light jet bomber for multiple roles, hoping to replace the Monarchy's fleet of older prop-driven tactical bombers.
Aero L.44
L.44
With the reliability of jet engines increasing and competition ever-so fierce, Aero tackled the challenge to design a next-generation fast-bomber, culminating into the L.44 fast bomber.
Avia-Dornier Do.19
Do.19
Lacking designs for strategic bombers, Avia purchased a number of Dornier four-engine bombers to showcase their potential to the air force.
Avia-Junkers Ju.290
Ju.290
Avia acquired a number of Ju.290 to supplement the small fleet of Do.19 in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.65
WM.65
Lázló Varga's four-engine bomber design was the first domestically-produced heavy bomber of its kind in the Empire.
Aero-Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16
FF.16
The German Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16 would be adopted as Austria's long-range bomber, locally produced by Aero Vodochody.
Weiss Manfréd WM.21
WM.21
Praga E.55
E.55
Aero A.204
A.204

$GER_transport_plane_equipment_1$

$GER_transport_plane_equipment_2$
$GER_transport_plane_equipment_2_short$
$GER_transport_plane_equipment_3$
$GER_transport_plane_equipment_3_short$
Henschel Erdkampfflugzeug 123
Hs 123
$GER_CAS_equipment_0_short$
One of the first designs created by the Henschel Flugzeugwerke the Hs 123 proved to be a formidable close-support attack aircraft. Quickly after defeating Fieseler in a design contest the Hs 123 was adopted by the air force thanks to its all metal construction and superior manoeuvrability. Fitted with a BMW 132Dc engine, it is capable of high speeds and nigh vertical dive bombing attacks. On the testing grounds it proved to be highly reliable and particularly easy to repair.
Henschel Träger-Sturzkampfbomber 123
Hs 123 T
$GER_cv_CAS_equipment_0_short$
Mainly due to its short wingspan and easy maintenance work, the Imperial Navy too decided against the Fi 98 and instead ordered the Hs 123. Used by both branches of the Heer, spare parts are easier and cheaper to acquire making the Hs 123 T, some armed with torpedoes, popular among the Admiralty.
Junkers 87
Ju 87
Junkers 87C
Ju 87C
The Ju 87C is a carrier-capable variant of the iconic Ju 87 Stuka dive bomber, specially designed for naval operations. Equipped with strengthened landing gear, arrestor hooks, and foldable wings for carrier storage, it retains the accuracy and fearsome dive-bombing capabilities of its land-based counterparts. The aircraft quickly earned a reputation for delivering precise strikes against enemy ships and coastal targets, becoming a cornerstone of the Imperial Navy's strike force
Henschel Erdkampfflugzeug 129
Hs 129
Having realised the need to upgrade from the outdated biplane design of the Hs 123, the Supreme Army Command ordered a new design for ground-attack airplanes. Designed for interdiction of materiel and logistics, the plane had to be thickly armoured for its low-level head-on strafing runs. While initially Henschel used a low power Argus engine it was later switched to a higher power BMW engine, eventually leading to serial production of the aircraft. Due to its high calibre cannon it is often referred to as 'Büchsenöffner' ('can opener') among the troops.
Junkers Ju 187 C
Ju 187 C
The Admiralty, having seen the successes of the Hs 129 developed a new iteration of land-based Ju 87. The new design, albeit focused on ground attacks, proved to work well for torpedo attacks and the thick armour makes the planes very durable against anti-aircraft fire and dogfights.
Dornier Jagdbomber 355
Do 355
Seeing the need to replace the old Henschel planes, the High Command ordered the design of new ground attack planes. Dornier, known for his exceptional designs, won the war ministry over, with this unorthodox but highly aerodynamic style. Unlike other planes the Do 355 has one propeller at the front and one at the back as well as its engine behind the cockpit which allows for higher performance and a better roll rate than other aircraft.
Blohm & Voss BV 155 T
BV 155 T/U-3
Having observed the superior agility and armament the BV 155 offers, the Imperial Navy decided to phase out it's older carrier variants and to invest in the development and construction of the new carrier based, light bomber aircraft.
Hb 132
Hb 132 T
Bf 1101/99
Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen Jagdflugzeug 68
Ff 68
Designed to replace the Ff 65, the Ff 68 met the most optimistic expectations in terms of handling and agility from the outset. Victory in a training battle against its main competitor Hb 51 finally confirmed the Ff 68 as the next German fighter. While now are mainly outdated planes (despite objections from the Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen side), they are still used as the night fighters by the German military.
Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen Träger-Jagdflugzeug 68
Ff 68 T
A well liked biplane, the Ff 68 was selected into service aboard the Kaiserliche Marine's aircraft carriers. Little modification was needed to make them suitable for carrier service, and much like their ground-based counterparts, it received high praise by carrier crews for its docile control characteristics.
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Jagdflugzeug 109
Bf 109
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke responded to a fighter tender with the modern mono-plane Bf 109 design. Despite the generally accepted point of view in German military circles that a fighter must necessarily be a biplane, the Bf 109 fighter, mounting the DB 600 engine, was accepted in service due to its heavier armament and significantly higher top speed compared with other designs, not to mention the ability of recovering from the spin almost at any time.
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Träger-Jagdflugzeug 109
Bf 109 T
With the significantly improved knowledge of aerodynamics and engine performance, the Kaiserliche Marine sent out contracts for a new carrier-borne aircraft. Unsurprisingly, they selected the Bf 109 that won the contract issued by the Heer. Modifications were made to ensure that it was carrier capable, including the wings and control surfaces being lengthened, fitting tailhooks and catapult fittings, as well as the implementation of foldable wingtips.
Focke-Wulf Jagdflugzeug 190
Fw 190
Difficulties to produce enough Daimler-Benz inline engines and successes of using radial engines in fighter designs by other nations, made the prospects of building a radial engine powered fighter promising. Developed by the personal initiative of Kurt Waldemar Tank, the chief engineer of Focke-Wulf, the Fw 190 design is notable for the survivability of the structure, ease of management, widespread use of modular assembly methods and ease of maintenance. Outperforming the still good Bf 109, but having child diseases of engine and concerning pilots with its armament, the new fighter was accepted in service after initial tests.
Focke-Wulf Träger-Jagdflugzeug 190
Fw 190 T
Due to limits of the Bf 109 airframe such as a weak and problematic gear leg, made a new fighter platform necessary and difficulties in developing the Bf 155 project means that producing a purpose-built carrier-borne fighter is out of the question. A conversion of the latest fighter aircraft, the Focke-Wulf Fw 190 was selected. Modifications were made, much like the Bf 109 T, fitting tailhooks and catapult fittings.
Focke-Wulf Jagdflugzeug 152
Fw 152
By early 1944, it became apparent that the development potential of the Fw 190 with the BMW 801 engine had dwindled. This became even more apparent with the advent of the new enemy fighters. A heavily modified Fw 190, the Fw 152 design development started in 1942 and has such features as increased fuel tanks alongside with speed and much heavier armament compared with the Fw 190. It's outstanding performance and ensuing popularity with the crews made it the poster child of Germany's air forces.
Blohm & Voss BV 155 T
BV 155 T
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Jagdflugzeug 262
Bf 262
Designed and created to replace older propeller-based aircraft the Bf 262 becomes the new poster child of our air force. One of the first of its type worldwide it is powered by two turbojet engines with which it can reach a higher speed than other conventional planes. The Air High Command has high hopes in the project, with the aim of eventually modernising the entire air fleet.
Bf 262 T
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Jagdflugzeug 1101
Bf 1101
$GER_jet_fighter_equipment_2_short$
Direct successor to the Bf 262, the design of the Bf 1101 includes a V-shaped body with sweepback wings. It is a single seat aircraft, powered by two Heinkel HeS 011 turbojet engines making it faster than the Bf 262 and featuring an improved throttle, greatly decreasing the chance of a compressor stall, which plagued its predecessor.
Do 22
Fieseler See-Mehrzweckflugzeug 167
Fi 167
Developed and built mainly for the use on carrier ships, the Fi 167 was also adopted by the Seeflieger of the Imperial Navy. Despite it's archaic looking design the biplane possesses great capabilities in agility due to its Benz & Cie engine. With its top speed of 325 km/h it forms the fast and heavy hitting core of the Küstenfliegergruppen.
Junkers 87D-4
Ju 87D-4
The Ju 87D-4 is a navalized variant of the Stuka, adapted for torpedo strikes against enemy ships. Equipped with carrier landing gear and a modified bomb rack for torpedoes, it combines deadly accuracy with reliable performance at sea. Its distinctive howl still strikes fear into naval crews as it dives for the kill.
Fokker Wasserflugzeug 80
Fk 80
After Anthony Fokker left with most of his firm for the Netherlands, the Imperial Army had to look for more politically reliable companies. This changed during the von Tirpitz chancellorship when Fokker reopened their plant in Germany and participated in design contests, eventually scoring a victory with the T.VIII. Called Fokker 80 by the German air force it is powered by a BMW 132 K and can carry bombs or torpedoes as heavy as 750 kilograms, making it a very formidable naval aviation aircraft.
Focke-Wulf Träger-Jagdflugzeug 190 T/U2
Fw 190 T/U2
A modified Focke-Wulf 190 T with the ability to carry heavy bombs or torpedoes
Blohm & Voss See-Mehrzweckflugzeug 194
Ha 194
Spiritual successor to the Ha 141, the Ha 194 kept the strangely asymmetrical design with the cockpit on the starboard side of the plane. Even though some air commanders are critical of the aircraft, it has proven to be highly agile and capable of travelling far distances without any stops.
Blohm & Voss BV 155 T/U-4
BV 155 T/U-4
Despite the relatively large wingspan of the airplane, the Ha 194 was also adopted by the Imperial Navy as carrier aircraft, mainly due to its high range as well as the short runway usage during landings and takeoffs.
Ho 229
Ho 229 T
Bf 1101/92
Do 23
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Zerstörer 110
Bf 110
Created as a heavy fighter aircraft with more range than the Bf 109, the Air Service conducted a competition which was won by the Bayerische Flugzeugwerke. Additionally to the advantage in range the armament of the Bf 110 is unusually strong - consisting of three 20mm cannons in the front. Even though less agile it proves to be an exceptional airplane, especially suited for use in our colonial holdings.
Junkers Zerstörer 88
Ju 88
Initially designed to be a fast bomber, the Ju 88 can fit into many roles, including air supremacy and interception missions. Chosen to succeed the Bf 110, it is more aerobatic and agile and capable of covering a larger air area than its predecessor.
Hansa-Brandenburg Zerstörer 219
Hb 219
Building on the strengths of the Ju 88, the designers at Hansa-Brandenburg designed the Hb 219. With superior air stability and higher agility the plane is able to better intercept and destroy enemy planes. Its newer engine and better aerodynamic construction allow for higher speeds and cover of greater ranges. The newly developed livery helps to disguise the plane better, making it harder for enemy fighters to spot it.
Ff 234B
Junkers Mittlerer Bomber 86
Ju 86
Ordered as bomber and airliner the Ju 86 is supposed to phase out any Tirpitz era planes within the Air Service. Due to its sturdy all metal construction and retractable main gear it has a very good handling and proves to be popular among pilots. It is widely used among other air forces around the world due to its excellent mid-air stability and good fuel consumption.
Hansa-Brandenburg Mittlerer Bomber 111
Hb 111
With the growing demand of bombers of Supreme High Command, Hansa-Brandenburg introduced the Hb 111 to support the Ju 86. With its Benz & Cie engine it is considerably faster and like its predecessor widely exported and used among many air forces around the world.
Dornier Bomber 217
Do 217
In order to replace the ageing Ju 86 and the Hb 111, the High Command ordered the production of a new generation of bombers. Designed as a naval bomber the Do 217 was replanned and transformed into a heavy bomber. Better armed than its successor and with the ability to perform dive bombing missions Dornier got the contract without facing competition.
Junkers Bomber 188
Ju 188
The Ju 188 was designed as a high performance bomber increasing the performance and the payload, following the outdated Ju 88. Even though the High Command is sceptical of the model, test pilots lauded it for its cockpit design. It is powered by two BMW engines and three propellers, significantly improving fuel efficiency and range.
Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen Strahlgetriebener Bomber 234
Ff 234
The development of jet engines had a great impact on the development of fighter and bomber aircraft. Among the first operational jet bombers in the world the Ff 234's great strength lies in its high speed. Faster than the usual propelled fighter plane it can outrun older enemy planes, making escapes of unguarded flights more likely. Despite its long takeoff runs it is highly aerobatic and favoured by pilots over propeller bombers.
Hansa-Brandenburg Strahlgetriebener Bomber 343
Hb 343
Even though the Ff 234 was a breakthrough in its field it still had a few issues. Among them were difficulties with the landing process and target bombing. However both aspects have been improved with the new generation, introduced by the Hb 343, creating an even faster, further reaching and more secure jet bomber.
Do P
Dornier Schwerer Bomber 19
Do 19
The Air Service was tasked with putting a bigger focus towards strategic bombing efforts. This led to a competition in which the Do 19 came out victorious. A heavy bomber, the Do 19, suffers from a lacklustre performance and little space for bombs, eventually becoming a stopgap product for the upcoming Hb 177.
Hansa-Brandenburg Schwerer Bomber 177
Hb 177
Designed and produced to replace the outdated Do 19, the Hb 177 features a far superior performance and armament as well as a spacious interior capable of carrying almost double the amount of bombs. It's all-metal construction proved to be sturdier and better to handle, albeit the big size of the plane still caused agility issues in test trials.
Hansa-Brandenburg Langstreckenbomber 277
Hb 277
Direct successor to the Hb 177, only little was changed. While the body remained the same, the biggest changes were the size of the wings and the engines. Instead of being powered by the often troublesome Benz & Cie engines, the Hb 277 featured BMW engines, increasing reliability and performance of the aircraft. The increased wingspan also makes the plane able to reach further away targets.
Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen Strahlgetriebener Bomber 555
Ff 555
Designed on the order of the Supreme High Command the Ff 555 is a long range flying wing jet bomber, built to be able to launch bombing campaigns in far away areas like the East Coast of North America and Asia East of the Urals. It's special V-form was chosen to allow for better aerodynamic flow to reach higher speeds.
Do 18
Do 24
BV 222
BV 238
BV 555
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Objektschutzjäger 163
Bf 163
Designed as a defensive aircraft to protect the airspace from enemy planes, the Bf 163 is truly a unique object. Powered by a rocket engine, the plane is supposed to climb up to high altitude, to then take on enemy bomber groups, while gliding back to the airfield. While the High Command is highly sceptical of the design and its risky tactics, some believe in it to be the air defence of the future.
Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Objektschutzjäger 263
Bf 263
With the Bf 163 showing its weaknesses the High Command has allowed the construction of a new rocket based interceptor model. The Bf 263 is made out of sturdier materials, a pressurised cockpit and a simpler and much more efficient engine, allowing for a doubled combat altitude and a much higher chance of survival for the pilot.
Fieseler Objektschutzjäger 349
Fi 349
Designed as a successor to the Bf 163 and the Bf 263, the Fi 349 tried to improve various shortcomings of the other interceptors. The aircraft only needs one pilot with basic training in aiming and firing, as it would be guided by an autopilot. Additionally after the attack the pilot does not need to return to an airstrip to land, but rather is ejected and lands with a parachute. This revolutionary design allows any common man to fly the plane should the need arise.
Do 16
Henschel Nahaufklärer 126
Hs 126
Tasked by the German Air Service, Henschel designed the Hs 126 as a high wing reconnaissance aircraft for short ranges. It is well received by pilots and the air command for its short takeoff and low speed capabilities, believed to be crucial for observation and intelligence gathering purposes.
Focke-Wulf Aufklärer 189
Fw 189
Winning a design competition against the Ff 198 and the Ha 141, Focke Wulf got the contract to replace the ageing Hs 126. The twin engine, twin boom, three seater tactical reconnaissance aircraft primarily operates on short distance flights. Its great manoeuvrability in dog fighting situations is praised by pilots.
Fw 191
Ff 234C
Junkers Transportflugzeug W 34
Ju W 34
The Junkers W 34 serves the Luftstreitkräfte as a light transport and utility aircraft, capable of carrying men, supplies, or communications equipment over reliable distances. Its sturdy all-metal construction and single-engine design make it simple to operate. It fulfills vital support duties that keep our forces supplied and mobile.
Junkers Transportflugzeug 52
Ju 52
Building upon the success of the Ju 34, the Junkers Ju 52 introduces a more modern design to meet the growing logistical demands of the armed forces. Its improved engines and significantly expanded cargo capacity allow for longer flights and heavier payloads, making it invaluable for supplying far-flung units across the Empire's territories.
Junkers Transportflugzeug 390
Ju 390
The Ju 390 is a true giant of the skies, developed to support long-range transport missions across the vast expanses of the Empire. With its extended range and massive payload capacity, it is particularly well-suited for long-range logistics and strategic operations. Despite its size, the aircraft maintains the reliability and robust engineering expected of Junkers designs.

Fokker D.XVII
D.XVII
Fokker D.XXI
D.XXI
The Fokker D.XXI was a low-wing monoplane fighter aircraft. It was designed in 1935 by Fokker around requirements laid out by the Royal Netherlands East Indies Army Air Force.\nThe main armament consisted of two pairs of 7.92mm M36 FN-Browning machine guns, two housed within the wings and the other pair within the forward fuselage, requiring the latter to shoot through the propeller blades; the fuselage guns carried 500 rounds each while the wing-mounted guns had 300 rounds each.
Koolhoven F.K.58
F.K. 58
The Koolhoven F.K.58 was a single engine, interceptor-fighter aircraft designed and manufactured by N.V. Koolhoven.\nIts armament consisted of 4 7.5mm guns. It had a retractable landing gear and was equipped with a more powerful 1080hp engine, allowing the plane to reach speeds of up to 505 km/h with an operational range of 750km.
De Schelde S.21
S.21
The De Schelde S.21 was a single-seat, single-engine, pusher monoplane designed by Koninklijke de Schelde N.V.\nThe S.21 was of all-metal construction, and featured an inverted gull wing, with the aircraft's tail carried on twin booms. The compact fuselage nacelle carried the pilot, engine and the aircraft's armament.\nArmament consisted of a single Madsen 23 mm cannon on a flexible mount in the nose and four 7.9 mm FN-Browning machine guns in the side of the nacelle.

Fokker T.VI (Ontwerp 115)
T.VI (Ontwerp 115)
Between August 1934 and February 1935, work began on the Ontwerp 115.\nThe Ontwerp 115 was of a four engined low-wing design with retractable landing gear and a twin rudder. The aircraft would have had four radial engines with performance calculated with the Gnome-Rhóne 14Krfs at 900Hp, the 14Krsd at 1110Hp, and the Wright Cyclone SFR-1820-F2 at 712Hp. The propellers would have been three bladed and adjustable in-flight. Bombing capacity was projected at two tonnes.
Hansa-Brandenburg Hb 177

Bayerische Flugzeugwerke Bf 264

Koolhoven F.K.51
F.K.51
Fokker F-XVIII
F-XVIII
Aero Vodochody A.101
A.101
Without any modern ground-attack aircraft, the Dual Monarchy sought to retrofit existing models to fit the role. The A.101 is the culmination of several attempts at upgrading the A.230 biplane to fill the role. Substantially larger and better armed than its predecessors, the A.101 is capable of both strafing and bombing as effectively as any of its contemporaries.
Weiss Manfréd WM.231
WM.231
Weiss Manfréd submitted the WM.23 fighter to compete with Avia's design. While its cowling-mounted, motor-driven Gebauer machine guns impressed the Committee, the B.135 was selected instead. Weiss Manfréd responded with a slight redesign, submitting it again as a dive-bomber instead to supplement the ageing fleet of A.101 biplanes in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.44
WM.44
Designed by László Varga, it was essentially a smaller, two-men version of the WM.31 series of heavy fighters and fast bombers. Like its predecessor, it was made out of both wood and metal to increase performance. It proved more than capable, albeit lightly-armoured, for close air support missions.
Phönix D.V
D.V
With the Weltkrieg's end, the Phönix company's planned redesign of its famous D.III biplane, with the expected designation 'D.IV', never came to pass. In 1931, however, the company would resurrect the D.IV moniker with the unveiling of an entirely new biplane featuring then cutting-edge specifications. An upgraded variant of the craft, designated D.V, was adopted by the Dual Monarchy in 1933.
Avia B.534
B.534
In 1932, Renowned Bohemian engineer František Novotný began work with the Avia company on a new all-metal biplane. This effort would culminate in the B-34, which was very nearly adopted by the Dual Monarchy over the Phönix. Not to be dissuaded, the Novotný redesigned the B-34 with a new engine and chassis, as well as a fully enclosed cockpit. Unlike its predecessor, this model, the B-534, would be adopted by the Dual Monarchy.
Avia B.135
B.135
After the success of its B-534 biplane, Avia soon began work on a cutting-edge monoplane which would ultimately culminate in the B-135. It used the Austro-Daimler V12D 860 hp engine and was equipped with a 20mm autocannon in the nose and two synchronised 8mm machine guns in the cowling, giving it great manoeuvrability and accurate fire.
Avia-Ikarus B.224
B.224
Essentially the final evolution of Novotný's design, with help from Kosta Sivčev as well as the Illyrian Ikarus company, the B.224's engine was upgraded the excellent 1000 hp Austro-Daimler V12E and the machine guns were replaced by two Gebauer 12.7mm motor-driven heavy machine guns, increasing its speed and firepower over its predecessor. Notable is the new bubble canopy for the pilot and sleek fuselage.
Avia Bf.262
Bf.262
Lagging behind in the development of jet fighters, Avia acquired a licence to produce the Bf 262 for the Fliegerkorps, replacing the German 30mm guns with locally-produced 20mm guns in their slightly-revised design.
Letov L.52
Letov L.52
L.52
L.52
When Austro-Daimler developed the U2 'Uzelac' engine, Letov produced a state-of-the-art jet fighter that would become the Monarchy's first local jet aircraft adopted into service.
Letov Š.328.v
Š.328.v
The Š.328.v was the seaplane derivative of the Š.28 series. It was armed with two forward-firing 8mm machine guns and two more in a flexible mount at the rear, and had a payload capacity of around 500kg.
Lohner-Fokker T.VIII W/C
T.VIII W/C
Lohner, a company that previously made seaplanes and flying boats for the k.u.k. Seefliegerkorps during the war, acquired the rights to produce the Fokker T.VIII for the Austro-Hungarian Navy.
Weiss Manfréd WM.442
WM.442
The WM.442 is the seaplane variant of the WM.44 made for the Seefliegerkorps, intended for Adriatic and Mediterranean anti-ship operations.
Praga E.51
E.51
Initially designed as a reconnaissance aircraft, it was quickly determined that the E.51 could be quickly adapted as a heavy fighter to counter strategic bombers.
Weiss Manfréd WM.31
WM.31
The Hungarian aviation engineer László Varga designed this 3-seat fighter around experimental gas turbine engines. However, technical difficulties arose over the engines and were replaced by two Austro-Daimler V12D instead. Notably, the WM.31 was of mixed construction.
Weiss Manfréd WM.50
WM.50
The WM.50 was a rather advanced designed for its time: The two engine push-pull configuration, twin-boom aircraft by Lázló Varga was designed to significantly improve the performance of two-engine fighters to counter high-altitude bombers.
Avia F.39
F.39
Originally developed by Fokker as a transport craft, the F.IX, the Avia company quickly saw the plane's military potential, and upon receiving a licence for the aircraft, redesigned the F.IX as a bomber, the F.39. The Dual Monarchy, lacking sufficient bombers, adopted the F.39 as a stopgap while newer models were developed.
Letov Š-50
Š-50
Intending to fill the Fliegerkorps' request for a multirole two-engine, three-man crew aircraft, Letov submitted the Š-50. However, the design did not catch interest and would never be produced, with Aero's design being eventually adopted instead.
Aero Vodochody A.300
A.300
This bomber design by Antonín Husník was, when it entered service, one of the fastest aircraft in inventory, only behind the newly-adopted B.135 fighter. Fast and with a good payload, it proved to be a versatile bomber and reconnaissance aircraft.
Weiss Manfréd WM.311
WM.311
The WM.31 was quickly adapted to perform the role of a fast, tactical bomber by weakening its offensive armament and improving its payload capacity.
Letov L.11
L.11
Based on a jet fighter design by the Bayerische Flugzeugwerke, the L.11 adapted the design into a fast and light jet bomber for multiple roles, hoping to replace the Monarchy's fleet of older prop-driven tactical bombers.
Aero L.44
L.44
With the reliability of jet engines increasing and competition ever-so fierce, Aero tackled the challenge to design a next-generation fast-bomber, culminating into the L.44 fast bomber.
Avia-Dornier Do.19
Do.19
Lacking designs for strategic bombers, Avia purchased a number of Dornier four-engine bombers to showcase their potential to the air force.
Avia-Junkers Ju.290
Ju.290
Avia acquired a number of Ju.290 to supplement the small fleet of Do.19 in service.
Weiss Manfréd WM.65
WM.65
Lázló Varga's four-engine bomber design was the first domestically-produced heavy bomber of its kind in the Empire.
Aero-Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16
FF.16
The German Flugzeugbau Friedrichshafen FF.16 would be adopted as Austria's long-range bomber, locally produced by Aero Vodochody.
Weiss Manfréd WM.21
WM.21

Aero A.204

SAI KZ IIA
KZ IIA
Within months of its founding, SAI, Skandinavisk Aero Industri, founded by two found technically proficient aircraft enthusiasts, produced two different sport planes. Their second model drew interest from the Danish military, which eventually contracted for the production of a ground attack variant on the craft.
